class="a-letter-space"></span><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" easy to install and no DirecTV installation fee</span></a></div><span class="a-color-secondary">         <span class="a-size-normal">     <span class="a-color-secondary">       By     </span>     <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/A32J41OITTUUFV/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/180-4347715-9852303" class="noTextDecoration">Bob</a>   </span> <span class="a-color-secondary"> on April 2, 2014</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R2YAD7UE8S2MW2" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>      <div class="a-section">   This worked great for me.  I already had 1 Genie Mini Wireless so I had the wireless bridge which made this one really easy to install.  Before buying it I called DirecTV to order one and they wanted to charge me for installation even though I would be installing it myself.  So I ordered it from Amazon, set it up myself and called them to activate it and they did not charge me any extra for activating it.  Also, they don&#8217;t want you to have more than 3 Genie Mini&#8217;s, but I now have 2 Genie Mini&#8217;s and 2 Genie Mini Wireless clients and they work great you just have to remember that only 3 will work at a time. </div>  </div>             <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="3" Please try again   </div></div></div> </span>    </div>            <div id="rev-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-RWY6Z1VJYBPJH" class="a-section celwidget"><div class="a-row a-spacing-micro"><span class="a-size-small a-color-secondary">8 of 8 people found the following review helpful</span><div class="a-icon-row a-spacing-none"><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" title="5.0 out of 5 stars" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RWY6Z1VJYBPJH/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/180-4347715-9852303?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B00IT8ZEMY&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><i class="a-icon a-icon-star a-star-5"></i></a><span class="a-letter-space"></span><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RWY6Z1VJYBPJH/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/180-4347715-9852303?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B00IT8ZEMY&nodeID=172282&store=electronics"><span class="a-size-base a-text-bold">Better than Wireless HDMI switches (And cheaper too)</span></a></div><span class="a-color-secondary">         <span class="a-size-normal">     <span class="a-color-secondary">       By     </span>     <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/A3D9V13PFS7J2Y/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/180-4347715-9852303" class="noTextDecoration">JDJeff</a>   </span> <span class="a-color-secondary"> on June 11, 2014</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-RWY6Z1VJYBPJH" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>      <div class="a-section">   I have used various wireless HDMI solutions over the years with varying degrees of success.  I bought this together with the wireless video bridge for a self install of a third client (other two are wired) for a Genie system.  While there are no directions included a quick google search will get you most of the way there.  In fact, the only difficulty I had was with Directv, which clearly is not yet ready for customer self installs.  The first person told me I had to have a professional installation.  Of course, by the time I called it was already completely set up and just needed activitation.  He sent me to level two support who couldn't find a way to activate the video bridge (it needs to be activated at the same time as the wireless client).  Finally took a supervisor to get it done and it works flawlessly.  Great picture, no lag, no dropouts, and used the pass through on the video bridge to connect one of the wired clients.  Only issue was range.  All green lights going from second floor to first, but couldn't get an adequate signal from third floor equipment room to 1st floor.  As mentioned I just put it behind one of the clients leaving 4 feet of RG6 between them (per a Directv Installer guide) and it worked well.  Also tried an alternative location but the connection from the splitter to that location was RG59 and it would not connect to the MOCA network.  In short, very stable connection, works as advertised with a minimum of fuss.  Just be patient and persistent with Directv in getting it activated.  Note that the video bridge has a beacon function to allow you to find a location for the bridge that will give you sufficient signal at the client.  Very helpful to get that right before completing all of the remaining steps for install.  Cheaper alternative than many of the very good wireless hdmi options as well. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="1" I acquired another tv and decided to put it in a room without coaxial. Did a little research and found DirecTV now offers a wireless solution. I ordered this box and the video bridge. Both items arrived super quick. I connected the video bridge to the SWM splitter (get this if you don't have one http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00BW60R68/ref=s9_simh_gw_p23_d0_i1?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=center-2&pf_rd_r=0G611922PDFZPHF9RQAX&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=1688200382&pf_rd_i=507846) and mounted this device behind my tv with velcro. Went into the main Genie box and followed the directions to add a receiver. I was able to successfully link the device. All that was left was call Directv to activate the box. Success HD over wireless. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0" Skip the wired mini C41.<br>I use a DIRECTV Genie HR44/700 (1TB) DVR and required DIRECTV Wireless Video Bridge (WVB). My DIY setup was not too difficult (followed instructions on DIRECTV site). If you have setup a wireless internet router you can setup a C41W without paying $100 for a DTV tech visit or the $49.00 service activation. DIRECTV call center Reps will not help with setup issues. The C41W box comes with a new RC71 RF remote, HDMI cable and power supply and basic installation instructions.<br>IMPORTANT NOTES:<br>1. Make sure you can provide at least 8 feet between the Genie HR44 (whole-house DVR), the Wireless Video Bridge (WVB), the Wireless Mini C41W (receiver - next room HDTV), and your Wireless Internet Router<br>2. Update C41W firmware via USB connection (minimum 6 foot USB cable) to your internet router before attempting to connect it to the HR44 Base DVR. The C41W will update automatically after connected; follow the C41W instructions on the new TV.<br>3. Setup the WVB: Using the HR44 DVR; Menu/Settings/Whole-Home/Video-Bridge. The WVB must be in discovery mode flashing Blue/Green before it will connect the C41W with the HR44 base DVR.<br>4. Setup Mini C41W: Use HR44 DVR; Menu/Settings/Whole-Home/Manage-Clients/Add-Client; copy the 4 digit PIN number displayed on HR44, enter it on the mini to sync the DVR. The WVB should go to steady Blue after it discovers the mini.<br>5. After all wireless equipment handshakes are complete call DIRECTV to activate the mini. Have the mini's serial number handy (bottom of unit).<br>6. My findings:<br>a.) Any and all Genie DIRECTV equipment, whether purchased thru an authorized dealer (weaKnees, etc.) or DIRECTV, require a new 2-Year contract.</span><span class="a-declarative" data-action="columnbalancing-showfullreview" data-columnbalancing-showfullreview="{&quot;rest&quot;:&quot; A verbal recorded commitment is required during the activation process;&lt;br /&gt;b.) The equipment is considered leased by DIRECTV - you do not own any of it. But the technology works, is reliable and provides great signal strength and picture quality.&quot;}"><a class="a-link-normal"
